    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',

        state: 'apple_oauth_state_8a9eb807-bd42-42e2-a59b-e700cd91519a'

<span id="freeTextContainer14644028540051425642"><i>"I won't tell anyone, Echo. I promise." Noah tucked a curl behind my ear. It had been so long since someone touched me like he did.   <span id="freeText14644028540051425642" style="display:none"><i>"I won't tell anyone, Echo. I promise." Noah tucked a curl behind my ear. It had been so long since someone touched me like he did. Why did it have to be Noah Hutchins? His dark brown eyes shifted to my covered arms. "You didn't do that-did you? It was done to you?" No one ever asked that question. They stared. They whispered. They laughed. But they never asked.</i><br /><br /><b>So wrong for each other...and yet so right.</b><br /><br />No one knows what happened the night Echo Emerson went from popular girl with jock boyfriend to gossiped-about outsider with "freaky" scars on her arms. Even Echo can't remember the whole truth of that horrible night. All she knows is that she wants everything to go back to normal. But when Noah Hutchins, the smoking-hot, girl-using loner in the black leather jacket, explodes into her life with his tough attitude and surprising understanding, Echo's world shifts in ways she could never have imagined. They should have nothing in common. And with the secrets they both keep, being together is pretty much<i> impossible</i>. Yet the crazy attraction between them refuses to go away. And Echo has to ask herself just how far they can push the limits and what she'll risk for the one guy who might teach her how to love again...</span>
  <a data-text-id="14644028540051425642" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

      </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer1790332269719528413"><b> “Fuck me and the rest of the world, I was in love.”<br/>— 	 Pushing the Limits, Katie McGarry </b><br/><br/>And I'm in love to, <br/><br/>I FUCKING LOVE THIS BOOK! <br/><br/>I FUCKING LOVE NOAH.<br/><br/>AND I FUCKING LOVE KATIE McGARRY! <br/><br/>I have officially read this only about, OH, a MILLION times. <br/><br/>How do you get sick of a book that draws you in from the first page every single time. There's so many different views of this book it's like reading a new story each and every time I read it. <br/><br/><b><br/>'His lips curved into a sexy smile and I became lost in </b></span>
  <span id="freeText1790332269719528413" style="display:none"><b> “Fuck me and the rest of the world, I was in love.”<br />— 	 Pushing the Limits, Katie McGarry </b><br /><br />And I'm in love to, <br /><br />I FUCKING LOVE THIS BOOK! <br /><br />I FUCKING LOVE NOAH.<br /><br />AND I FUCKING LOVE KATIE McGARRY! <br /><br />I have officially read this only about, OH, a MILLION times. <br /><br />How do you get sick of a book that draws you in from the first page every single time. There's so many different views of this book it's like reading a new story each and every time I read it. <br /><br /><b><br />'His lips curved into a sexy smile and I became lost in him. “I love you, Echo Emerson.”<br />I whispered the words as he brought his lips to mine. “Forever.”'<br /></b><br /><br />This book is just, there's no words. <br /><br />It's so friggin awesome, I am going to have to worship it.<br /><br />No-one can possibly understand how obsessed I am with this whole story!<br /><br />I have been waiting to read this for months, and boy was it worth the wait. <br /><br /><b> "“I’M BUYING YOU A COAT.” And I meant it. I opened the car door and slung my leather jacket around her shoulders. “It’s February. Why don’t you ever have a damn jacket on?”<br />Echo slid her arms through my coat, closing her eyes as she inhaled. When she finally opened them, she fluttered her eyelashes, giving me a look of pure seduction. “Maybe I like wearing yours instead.”<br />I swallowed. I had plans, and those plans did not involve kissing her against my car. Dammit, she was going to kill me. “Congratulations, it’s yours.”<br />Her laughter warmed me in ways a jacket couldn’t. “Are you going to be a big pushover now?”<br />Appeared so. I entwined my fingers with Echo’s and walked her across the empty street, toward the fountain. Red and pink lights lit up the water trickling from the three flowered tiers.<br />“It’s beautiful.” Echo stared at the fountain, her eyes darting to the different flowers etched in the metal. No, she was beautiful.</b> <br /><br /><br />Noah is just, AHHHH The things I would do to him<br />He is just so damn attractive. He may as well put a collar and lead on me because I would be his 'pet' anyday! <br /><br />Echo is just amazing. Sarcastic, gorgeous and feisty. She and me were besties from the first sentence. <br />Amazing heroin. <br />People would constantly be asking her if she was 'ok', and instead of lying and saying 'fine' like the other millions of people out there she says this: <br /><br />“My father is a control freak, I hate my stepmother, my brother is dead and my mother has … well … issues. How do you think I’m doing?”<br /><br />I laughed and I knew I was going to love every minute of this book. <br /><br /><br />I love the way the author split Noah and Echo's POV's. They were perfectly timed.<br />So well written and addictive. <br />Theres so much more I could say about this book, but right now I'm like a drug addict and this book is my crack. I've spent too long writing this and now I'm shaking to get back and quite possibly read it all over again. <br />I know it's only come out today but damn I'd have to advise you to drop whatever it is your reading and start with this because my friggin god you will not be able to PUT IT DOWN. <br /><br />The story that lies in between the covers are sad, emotional, lovely, sweet, romantic and breathtakingly heartwarming. <br /><br />My heart aches and grieves for both Noah and Echo, whom have lived such hard and sad lives and have had to grow up so fast and make descisions people as young as themselves shouldn't have to make. Hell their my age and I don't know what I would have done in their positions. <br /><br />They are so admirable and anyone would be lucky to have them as role models. Their strong, loyal, honest and good people who just needed guidance and Mrs Collins was there supporting them the whole way through she never gave up. <br /><br />My god, I loved this. I can't tell you how much I love this. <br /><br />There's not one bad point I can think of. And that NEVER happens. Not to me. I'm so fussy and will pick over the littlest things. But this is the exception. And I wouldn't have it any other way.<br /><br /><br />Un-freakin-believable- that's the first word that came to mind when I finished this. This book blew me away and this has definitely barged its way into my top 10. This book is worth 5 big fat stars and I am now going to go and make it known to everyone about how much they should read it.<br /><br /><br />Here's some More of my favorite parts;<br /><br /><b> <br /><br />My song ended, my finger stopped tapping the beat, and we ceased swaying from side to side. She held perfectly still, keeping her hand in mine, her head resting on my shoulder. I nuzzled into the warmth of her silky curls, tightening my hold on her. Echo was becoming essential, like air.<br /><br /><br /><br />She opened her mouth, her tongue seductively touching mine, almost bringing me to my knees. Flames licked through me as our kiss deepened. Her hands massaged my scalp and neck, only stoking the heat of the fire.<br /><br /><br /><br />“Because,” I said as I felt the familiar twisting in my stomach. “You saw me lose it. You saw me almost go insane.”<br />The muscles in his shoulders visibly tensed. “I watched you battle against the worst memory of your life and I watched you win. Make no mistake, Echo. I battled right beside you. You need to find some trust in me … in us.”<br />Noah inhaled and slowly let the air out. His stance softened and so did his voice. “If you’re scared, tell me. If you need to cry and scream, then do it. And you sure as hell don’t walk away from us because you think it would be better for me. Here’s the reality, Echo: I want to be by your side. If you want to go to the mall stark naked so you can show the world your scars, then let me hold your hand. If you want to see your mom, then tell me that, too. I may not always understand, but damn, baby, I’ll try.”<br />I stared at him and he stared at me. <br /><br />It doesn’t get better,” I said. “The pain. The wounds scab over and you don’t always feel like a knife is slashing through you. But when you least expect it, the pain flashes to remind you you’ll never be the same.”<br /><br />This book is just so intensely real. <br /><br /></b> I could just read this over and over and <i> over </i> again. </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer16729172999196039016"><b><br/>Noah <3<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380735767ra/3116863.gif' alt='Image Hosted by ImageShack.us' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><br/><blockquote><i>"Luke used to give me butterflies. <br/>Noah spawned mutant pterodactyls."</i></blockquote>
<br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380417651i/826313.jpg' alt='Image Hosted by ImageShack.us' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><br/><br/><br/>This was such a sweet and heartbreaking story, with both MCs having some serious problems, but I still loved it <3<br/>I am not a fan of angst and drama, and there is both here, but not too much, so I don't think it'll be a problem for anyone else :DD<br/><br/><br/><br/>A few things you need to know:<br/><br/><br/><br/>1. What the book is about</b><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380417651i/826314.jpg' alt='Image Hosted by ImageShack.us' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><br/>A bad boy and a troubled girl are forced to work together to solve their problems, and in the meantime they manage to fall</span>
  <span id="freeText16729172999196039016" style="display:none"><b><br>Noah &lt;3<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380735767ra/3116863.gif" alt="Image Hosted by ImageShack.us" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br><blockquote><i>"Luke used to give me butterflies. <br>Noah spawned mutant pterodactyls."</i></blockquote>
<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380417651i/826313.jpg" alt="Image Hosted by ImageShack.us" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br><br><br>This was such a sweet and heartbreaking story, with both MCs having some serious problems, but I still loved it &lt;3<br>I am not a fan of angst and drama, and there is both here, but not too much, so I don't think it'll be a problem for anyone else :DD<br><br><br><br>A few things you need to know:<br><br><br><br>1. What the book is about</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380417651i/826314.jpg" alt="Image Hosted by ImageShack.us" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br>A bad boy and a troubled girl are forced to work together to solve their problems, and in the meantime they manage to fall in love &lt;3<br>Echo is trying to remember a repressed memory from the night she almost died, and Noah is doing whatever he can to get custody of his brothers.<br>I won't say more cause you just have to read to find out :)<br>Anyway, there are both POVs in this book, and I really love that :))<br>I'll talk more about Noah and Echo in their sections :)<br><br><br><br><b>2. Something about Echo</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380417651ra/826315.gif" alt="Image Hosted by ImageShack.us" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br>She has terrible scars on her arms, and doesn't remember how she got them. She isn't doing well and has to go to counseling with her family.<br>She is an outcast in school ever since the "incident", her friends have given up on her and she isn't the popular one with a hot boyfriend anymore.<br>She is desperate to find out what happened to her that night, and unwillingly makes a deal with Noah, a student she's been tutoring, to get both their files from the school counselor.<br><br><br><br><b>3. Something about Noah</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380417651ra/826316.gif" alt="Image Hosted by ImageShack.us" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br>He is very mature for his age, but it isn't surprising considering everything that's happened to him.<br>After the death of his parents, he got into foster care and of course, it didn't go well. Now he's a bad boy with a bad reputation, but all he really wants is to get his brothers in his custody the moment he turns 18. <br>The best way to do that is to excel in school, so he starts the tutoring lessons with Echo. <br><br><br><br><b>4. Noah and Echo</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380417651ra/826317.gif" alt="Image Hosted by ImageShack.us" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br>I love them together &lt;3<br>They are perfect for one another, and I loved every scene they had &lt;3<br>Anyway, Echo's remembering was really, REALLY tough to read, and I am so glad Noah was there to support her most of the way &lt;3<br>Noah and his family - I knew how it would end, and it's the way it's supposed to be (although a bit idyllic but oh well :D).<br>Noah gave me butterflies like he did to Echo, he's sweet and swoony even though he's a bad boy :D <br>Loved the scene when he meets her father and takes her to his place &lt;3<br><br><br><br><b>5. It made me cry</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380417651ra/826318.gif" alt="Image Hosted by ImageShack.us" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br>There were a few very sad scenes, but one hit me most, and it didn't have anything to do with Noah/Echo. <br>It was about Noah and his little brothers, the scene when <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Jacob won an award for writing a story about Noah. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br>I actually had to take a break to compose myself and get rid of the tears XD and when I started reading the scene again, I started crying again so I had to compose again LMAO :D<br>Yes I'm a weeper, but mostly I just get misty-eyed, this was full-on crying! Gah. Anyway. I think that scene is my favorite from the book :)))<br><br><br><br><b>6. No sex in this one, not even a fade-out :D</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380417651ra/826319.gif" alt="Image Hosted by ImageShack.us" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br>And you know what? It didn't bother me AT ALL :)<br>In fact, it would probably be icky for me to read about teenagers having sex ahahahahah so yeah, the glances, the kisses, the touches, I swooned at that and didn't even need the sex :DDDD<br><br><br><br><br><br><br><b>And so, this is a great book, I really enjoyed it, and I can't wait to read more from this series :)))</b><br><br><br><br><br><br><br></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

</a><br/><br/>♦ This is a story about a boy with a past in ashes who fell in love wit</span>
  <span id="freeText3958926661968009906" style="display:none"> Holy Sh—<br>Oh, my---<br>What the---<br>For the love of---<br>Sweet baby---<br><br><i> MOTHERFUCKER! </i> This book was <b>fabulous</b>/<i>great</i>/<b>wow</b>/fan♦freaking♦tastic!<br><br>*deep breath*<br><br>I would just like to go on the record and THANK Katie McGarry for creating Noah Hutchins. And for creating a book that held me captive until the wee hours of the morning. Holy SHIT! Your book’s good, ma’am.<br><br>So without further ado… Allow me to introduce you to “Pushing the Limits”… ;)<br><br><a href="http://s59.photobucket.com/user/ashleeporte/media/tumblr_mlkr3tv1K21rtxj3eo1_r1_500.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380413203i/813248.jpg" alt=" photo tumblr_mlkr3tv1K21rtxj3eo1_r1_500.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>♦ This is a story about a boy with a past in ashes who fell in love with a girl whose memory was consumed by what she couldn’t remember. ♦<br><br><a href="http://s59.photobucket.com/user/ashleeporte/media/tumblr_mj3z86NZRn1rtxj3eo1_500.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">

</a><br><br>♥ <i>
  <u> Echo </u>
</i> ♥<br><br><a href="http://s59.photobucket.com/user/ashleeporte/media/60b41b30c09448094978ef951fc24a01.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380413203i/813250._SY540_.jpg" alt=" photo 60b41b30c09448094978ef951fc24a01.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><b>
  <i> Young girl, tragically scarred, attempts to return to her normal life, only to find out her normal life doesn’t want her back. </i>
</b><br><br>With nothing but stained-glass memories, the only thing Echo knows is that her mother tried to kill her two years ago. Her mother was beautiful, and had every talent known to a paintbrush.<br><br>Just like Echo.<br><br>But Echo doesn’t remember that night two years ago. She doesn’t remember her mother trying to kill her, and the last time she tried to recall those memories; she landed in the hospital due to mental trauma for trying to force her mind to bring up something it was trying desperately to repress.<br><br><a href="http://s59.photobucket.com/user/ashleeporte/media/tumblr_ml683pFBkw1rtxj3eo1_500.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380413203i/813251.jpg" alt=" photo tumblr_ml683pFBkw1rtxj3eo1_500.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Her dad knows what happened. <br>Her step-mother knows what happened.<br>Even Echo’s highschool <i>counselor</i> knows what happened.<br><br>But no one’s fessing up. Everyone wants Echo to remember on her own. <br><br>So without those memories, Echo sticks to the facts:<br><br>•	Her mother <i> did </i> try to kill her, and she has the physical scars to prove it.<br>•	She’s now the school freakshow.<br>•	Her father cheated on her mother with Echo’s baby-sitter.<br>•	Her best friend of an older brother is dead.<br>•	And she’s falling fast and hard for someone who she should stay the hell away from.<br><br>♥ <i>
  <u> Noah </u>
</i> ♥<br><br><a href="http://s59.photobucket.com/user/ashleeporte/media/naver_com_20120816_095821.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380413203i/813252._SX540_.jpg" alt=" photo naver_com_20120816_095821.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><i>
  <b> This was Noah Hutchins. The Noah Hutchins that refused steady relationships or even dating. The Noah Hutchins that only wanted one-night stands. A stoner. My opposite. And right now, everything I wanted. </b>
</i><br><br>His past went up in flames. Literally. And it took his parents along with it, leaving him with nothing but once-a-month visitation rights to his younger brothers.<br><br>And Noah would give <i>anything</i> to have his brothers back. <br><br>But when you’re a teenager thrown into the foster system… it’s hard to live life on the straight and narrow.<br><br>It doesn’t matter that he was once at the top of his class. It doesn’t matter that he was an MVP on the basketball team. It doesn’t matter that at one time in his life, smiling was once just a reflex kind of thing.<br><br>All he has now are girls who only seem to remember his name when they’re moaning it; a family who consists of two friends he would do anything for; an annoying high school counselor who for some unknown fucking reason, believes in him; two younger brothers with smiles that he would literally move heaven and hell for; and…<br><br>An irritatingly gorgeous red-head tutor who has scars on the outside that perfectly match the ones he carries on the inside.<br><br>And despite everything, Noah can’t help falling in love with her.<br><br><a href="http://s59.photobucket.com/user/ashleeporte/media/41b1e71eb4f0b50c3453fc358c057cfc.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">

  <i> Soon the pen she held in her hand drummed in time with her foot. I understood her rhythm. That feeling of everything inside twisting to the point that if you didn’t find a release you’d explode. I craved to grant her peace. </i>
</b><br><br><a href="http://s59.photobucket.com/user/ashleeporte/media/ceb3471ea60d56e473259c49dfb16c02.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">

</a><br><br><i>
  <b>I wanted to blow her mind with every touch and every kiss so her very thought always came back to me. I would never touch anyone else again without thinking about her. </b>
</i><br><br>But sometimes…<br><br>No matter how hard you try to fix someone;<br>No matter how hard you fight their demons;<br>No matter how hard you guard their sleep;<br><br><a href="http://s59.photobucket.com/user/ashleeporte/media/tumblr_mg9c1qTnXv1rtxj3eo1_500.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">

</a><br><br>You can’t. <br></span>

<div id="review_304237116" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/304237116" />
    <a title="Stacia (the 2010 club)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4013351-stacia-the-2010-club"><img alt="Stacia (the 2010 club)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1417661051p2/4013351.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/304237116?book_show_action=true">Mar 31, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Stacia (the 2010 club)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Stacia (the 2010 club)" href="/user/show/4013351-stacia-the-2010-club">Stacia (the 2010 club)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4013351-stacia-the-2010-club?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4013351-stacia-the-2010-club?shelf=drama-llama">drama-llama</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4013351-stacia-the-2010-club?shelf=contemporary-romance">contemporary-romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer304237116" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2815503225925065206"><b>
  <blockquote>
    <i>Normal. She wanted normal and so did I.</i>
  </blockquote>
</b><br/>If I could summarize this book with one (okay, technically two) sentence, that would be the one. Nothing else needs to be said. You can figure out from one simple sentence that this is a book about two people who have lost everything and are trying to figure out how to get normalcy back in their lives. <br/><br/><b>3.25 stars.</b> If I was judging <i>Pushing the Limits</i> solely based on the journey of the characters and how they struggled to reach their own personal </span>
  <span id="freeText2815503225925065206" style="display:none"><b>
  <blockquote>
    <i>Normal. She wanted normal and so did I.</i>
  </blockquote>
</b><br />If I could summarize this book with one (okay, technically two) sentence, that would be the one. Nothing else needs to be said. You can figure out from one simple sentence that this is a book about two people who have lost everything and are trying to figure out how to get normalcy back in their lives. <br /><br /><b>3.25 stars.</b> If I was judging <i>Pushing the Limits</i> solely based on the journey of the characters and how they struggled to reach their own personal victories, I would have gone 4 stars on the book. This was a great story. I like to see characters with depth and grit. It's always fascinating to watch people push past their inner demons and come out on the other side to start their healing process. Both Noah and Echo were inspirational characters who learned not only how to work on themselves, but also learned how to encourage each other to trust again.<br /><br /><b>What lost me (just a little) was the execution.</b><br /><i>There were several trigger words and generalizations which had me cringing :</i><br /><br />1. The over-use of nicknames, such as baby, siren, goddess, nymph, etc., as well as the <i>always-sure-to-cause-an-eye-roll</i> note of likening another person's presence to a drug. As well, the mention of Echo smelling like cinnamon was excessive after about the third time. <i>She smells like a bakery. I got it.</i> <br /><br />2. Stating that foster kids and kids from bad homes lay low for a reason (this is a stereotype that isn't always true - I've known kids from foster homes and bad homes who were popular and good students). Statements like this always seem to make me want to cue the dramatic music in my head because these appear to be written for the purpose of trying to invoke a feeling which isn't always necessary.<br /><br />3. Assuming that someone is on a bad path because they smoke weed or drink socially, and therefore that person needs to expel this from their life immediately, otherwise their entire future is in danger. <i>Well crap...I feel bad for more than 50% of today's teens then.</i> They're all screwed. It's a wonder I have such a productive life today, being a former weed smoker and social drinker.<br /><br />4. Using the word "forever" to describe a fledgling relationship. <i>Did Judy Blume teach us nothing?</i> This is HIGH SCHOOL. Yes, some people meet their spouses in high school... but I hate when books want to predict futures which aren't necessarily predictable. Anything can happen after high school. We don't need to tie these kids down beyond possibly continuing the relationship into college. Not unless you're going to do a <i>Perfect Chemistry</i> epilogue where it shows them married years down the line (and believe me, I could live without those).<br /><br /><b>What really did shine about this book :</b><br /><br />1. The characters. Both Echo and Noah were smart and cautious about many things. Echo was a great example of showing how it's okay not to have sex if you're not ready. Noah was a great example of how a teenage guy can be horny and hormonal and wanting to get laid, yet still respectful of a girl's wishes if he cares about her. His honesty was refreshing. He didn't stop wanting sex, even though he let Echo have her space when she needed it.<br /><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>Her beautiful breasts were right there for me to see, but I wanted to do more than observe, I wanted to...</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br />2. As mentioned earlier, the story. Other than it being a little on the long side and having a few moments I could have lived without, I enjoyed the read. The story did have a few similarities to <i>Perfect Chemistry</i> but wasn't an exact mirror either, so I wasn't bothered by it. The problems of the main characters in <i>Pushing</i> were not gang related, yet the problems were still just as emotional and tough as what Alex and Brittany had to go through in PC. <br /><br />Overall, I think this would be a good read for people who are huge fans of love conquering the greatest of problems.<br /><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>"I watched you battle against the worst memory of your life and I watched you win. Make no mistake, Echo. I battled right beside you."</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="2815503225925065206" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_321525891" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/321525891" />
    <a title="Emily May" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may"><img alt="Emily May" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528390751p2/4622890.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/321525891?book_show_action=true">Apr 30, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily May" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily May" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may">Emily May</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=2012">2012</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=romance">romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer321525891" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4000813946655979655"><a href='http://thebookgeek.co.uk' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1379777457i/368079.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/>When I rate a book three stars, it usually means indifference, that the book was neither especially good or bad. That I probably won't even remember it in a few days time. With <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10194514.Pushing_the_Limits' title='Pushing the Limits by Katie McGarry' rel='nofollow noopener'>Pushing the Limits</a> that is not the case, it's more that I feel the positives and negatives equally balance each other out and the overall book falls somewhere in the middle of the rating scale because of it. I will say, though, the issues that I felt sure I'd have with it were not the reason I gave it such an average </span>
  <span id="freeText4000813946655979655" style="display:none"><a href="http://thebookgeek.co.uk" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1379777457i/368079.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br>When I rate a book three stars, it usually means indifference, that the book was neither especially good or bad. That I probably won't even remember it in a few days time. With <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10194514.Pushing_the_Limits" title="Pushing the Limits by Katie McGarry" rel="nofollow noopener">Pushing the Limits</a> that is not the case, it's more that I feel the positives and negatives equally balance each other out and the overall book falls somewhere in the middle of the rating scale because of it. I will say, though, the issues that I felt sure I'd have with it were not the reason I gave it such an average rating.<br><br>I approached this young adult romance with the caution I always approach young adult romance novels with. Plus an extra shot of it because of the bad boy/good girl cliche we are promised. As far as these types of cliched stories go, I'd say <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10194514.Pushing_the_Limits" title="Pushing the Limits by Katie McGarry" rel="nofollow noopener">Pushing the Limits</a> is one of the best and is far better than those of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/274533.Simone_Elkeles" title="Simone Elkeles" rel="nofollow noopener">Simone Elkeles</a>. I personally think McGarry has written a great debut and the novel would have fully achieved excellence had she not played in the safe zone and used the same old format and character types. Everything was a little too predictable. However, I see enough promise here to want to try her next novel - <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13561164.Dare_You_To" title="Dare You To by Katie McGarry" rel="nofollow noopener">Dare You To</a> - and see if Beth's story can avoid the same mistakes (based on her character, I think it might).<br><br>So... bad boys. Just a few years ago, I wouldn't have hesitated to say that I love a bad boy. The kind of man who promises a wild adventure with his smile, and exciting sexcapades with a raise of his eyebrow. But the definition of this sexy creature has changed, or perhaps it was always the same and I just didn't notice it as much... but either way, a "bad boy" is now someone like Patch Cipriano from <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6339664.Hush__Hush__Hush__Hush___1_" title="Hush, Hush (Hush, Hush, #1) by Becca Fitzpatrick" rel="nofollow noopener">Hush, Hush</a> and others like him, men or boys who push women around, attempt to control them, become violent when they don't get their own way. Noah Hutchins is nothing like that. Noah is what I mean when I say "bad boy", he is fun and likes to break a few rules, but he always respects Echo's wishes, he is kind to her and - you won't believe it - actually leaves her alone when she metaphorically gives him the finger.<br><br>To get down to the real problem, it is quite simply: the angst. McGarry is a good enough author to realise that she needs to give her characters issues and imperfections (especially if they're going to be of the cliche variety). But I didn't think the execution of either character dealing with their problems was done well, it felt a bit messy, a lot melodramatic, and it was all wrapped up in what I felt was a rather unsatisfactory way. I also think the sizzling chemistry quickly gave way to the usual romantic natterings of the deeply forever in luuurrrve. Don't get me wrong, I wanted Echo and Noah to be together right up to the last minute, but I would have preferred a little less "I love you more than anything in the world, baby". There's only so many times calling someone "baby" is cute.<br><br>In the end, this book had two characters with amazing chemistry who I genuinely cared about. They were flawed and interesting, but there was too much doom, gloom and angsting going on. Some parts were sad until I passed through the sadness and into eye-rolling territory. I feel conflicted about the novel as a whole, but I do believe in the author's potential. Let's see where she goes from here.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4000813946655979655" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2677573993" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2677573993" />
    <a title="peachygirl" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/51435362-peachygirl"><img alt="peachygirl" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1555561561p2/51435362.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2677573993?book_show_action=true">Jan 17, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="peachygirl" class="user" itemprop="url" name="peachygirl" href="/user/show/51435362-peachygirl">peachygirl</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/51435362-peachygirl?shelf=read-in-2019">read-in-2019</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2677573993" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12789329843267435270">This is the story of a former popular girl and golden boy finding each other in their quest for different lives and freedom, after they've lost everything that mattered.<br/>Echo Emerson has lost her dad to her nanny turned step-mother, her mum to bipolar disorder, her brother to the Marines and her friends and social life to one terrible night that gave her deep physical and psychological scars. She's erased the night from her memory to the point where flashes of those painful hours make her questio</span>
  <span id="freeText12789329843267435270" style="display:none">This is the story of a former popular girl and golden boy finding each other in their quest for different lives and freedom, after they've lost everything that mattered.<br />Echo Emerson has lost her dad to her nanny turned step-mother, her mum to bipolar disorder, her brother to the Marines and her friends and social life to one terrible night that gave her deep physical and psychological scars. She's erased the night from her memory to the point where flashes of those painful hours make her question her sanity.<br />I admit, I'm not really generous with sympathy for angst-ridden teens, but Echo's story shook me. She was dealt with so many consequent shitty cards, I didn't know which one to feel bad for. For all his claims of love for his daughter, Echo's dad could have been there for her better instead of hiding behind his guilt and his young wife's pregnant tummy. Not touching the topic of the human wrecking ball that is Echo's mom. And some of her 'friends' woke my inner bitch up with the urge to slap them. Repeatedly. Everything was made doubly worse by Echo's authority issues, as she put it and her ridiculous people pleasing tendencies. <br />Noah Hutchins has lost his parents in a fire accident, his brothers to the foster care system and himself to the need for making his family whole again. His distrust of adults was understandable but his insta connection to Echo made no sense to me, given his guarded nature. There was attraction in the beginning, yes. To some extent, I'd even say they were kindred spirits. But there was absolutely no chemistry. Nada. The romance scenes seemed forced and mechanical. They would have been better off as friends. But the plot would have taken a hit, so I'm gonna let that one go. Some of the scenes involving Noah's interaction with his brothers were extremely moving. And I really liked Mrs.Collins. She was the only decent adult in this book. <br />I'd recommend this book for YA fans, but not if you're looking for an epic romance or a swoon-worthy love story. I'm looking forward to read Isaiah's story though. Biker chick Beth was an absolute delight!</span>
  <a data-text-id="12789329843267435270" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_354957669" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/354957669" />
    <a title="Aestas Book Blog" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5604583-aestas-book-blog"><img alt="Aestas Book Blog" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1353371225p2/5604583.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/354957669?book_show_action=true">Jun 24, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Aestas Book Blog" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Aestas Book Blog" href="/user/show/5604583-aestas-book-blog">Aestas Book Blog</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5604583-aestas-book-blog?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer354957669" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3687145281925084750">4.5 stars<br/><br/>A heart-wrenching YA book about two broken teens struggling to put the shattered pieces of their lives back together and finding love along the way.<br/><br/><i> <b> “Her shoulders never shook. No tears streamed down her face. The worst type of crying wasn’t the kind everyone could see–the wailing on street corners, the tearing at clothes. No, the worst kind happened when your soul wept and no matter what you did, there was no way to comfort it. A section withered and became a scar on the part of your </b></i></span>
  <span id="freeText3687145281925084750" style="display:none">4.5 stars<br><br>A heart-wrenching YA book about two broken teens struggling to put the shattered pieces of their lives back together and finding love along the way.<br><br><i> <b> “Her shoulders never shook. No tears streamed down her face. The worst type of crying wasn’t the kind everyone could see–the wailing on street corners, the tearing at clothes. No, the worst kind happened when your soul wept and no matter what you did, there was no way to comfort it. A section withered and became a scar on the part of your soul that survived. For people like me and Echo, our souls contained more scar tissue than life.” </b> </i><br><br>From the first line of this book, I was drawn right into Echo’s world. With a mentally ill mother, an overly controlling father, and her beloved older brother dead, Echo’s life is far from perfect. Its stifling. And you can totally feel it. The story just grabs at your heart strings.<br><br>Noah was an amazing character. He’s a bad boy, but only on the outside. He seems to be that way because that’s what everyone in his life labels him as. A stoner, one-night-stand player, under achiever… thats how the world sees him. But no one sees what led him to become this way. To the depths of his pain and the tragedy of the events in his life.<br><br><i> “ …I could tell he was looking at me. The stubble on his face moved as he smiled. Noah had muscles, looks, and trouble stalking him. Somehow he made jeans and a t-shirt look dangerous. Not that I was into girl-using stoners. Yet, I took another peek at him while sipping my drink.” </i><br><br>He really stole my heart – like all the way! His parents died in an accident a few years back and he and his little brothers were put into the foster system and separated and now he is fighting to get them out of the system and to put whats left of his family back together. Every SINGLE one of his scenes with his little brothers made my cry (a lot) and just made my heart ache with wanting them to be happy.<br><br>Both Noah and Echo are intensely angry and miserable in their lives, honestly it was hard to say which one made my heart break more at times. This book is so well written that you understand their frustrations and anger at the systems and rules which are screwing up their lives as though they were your own.<br><br>The book is told in alternating POVs with serves to show how different the worlds they come from are. The romantic relationship in this book builds slowly. Its not an undeniable- love-at-first-sight-instant-relationship kind of book. The personal journeys of the characters are the main focus of the storyline although they do end up together Both of them have been betrayed by life, and watching them learn to trust each other was really sweet.<br><br><i> <b> “If you’re scared, tell me. If you need to cry and scream, then do it. And you sure as hell don’t walk away from us because you think it would be better for me. Here’s the reality, Echo: I want to be by your side. If you want to go to the mall stark naked so you can show the world your scars, then let me hold your hand. If you want to see your mom, then tell me that too. I may not always understand, but damn, baby, I’ll try.” </b> </i><br><br>The issues this book deals with are very serious. Abuse. Neglect. Truth. Lies. Love. Healing. The intensity of the bond between siblings. There is nothing lighthearted about this book. Its deeply, gut-wrenchingly emotional. As I was reading, I’d literally have to take mini breathers to calm my heart between some of the scenes.<br><br><i> ”Tell me you chose me, Echo.”…<br>“I chose you.”…<br>“You will never regret it. I promise.” </i><br><br>I think fans of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13372690.Slammed__Slammed__1_" title="Slammed (Slammed #1) by Colleen Hoover" rel="nofollow noopener">Slammed</a> might like this book. It’s by no means the same storyline, but it shares a similar feeling. Although its more 'tame'… very strongly YA.<br><br>There were a few things that bugged me a little about the book. Echo’s reliance on her ‘popular’ friends at school and her need for their approval didn’t really sit right with me… but at the same time, I guess it was an understandable feeling for someone in high school. I just wish it hadn’t been so important to her…. And I also would have wished for an epilogue. The book has a happy-for-now ending (and a sequel featuring some of the secondary characters on the way) but after all the heart ache in the book, I still would have liked a glimpse maybe 5 years into the future so see how things had worked out for them.<br><br>All in all though, I really loved this read… if you are looking for a new YA book, this is it!<br><br>How I see Noah and Echo:<br><br><img width="100%" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380381827i/739267._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>For more of my reviews, visit <a href="http://aestasbookblog.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Aestas Book Blog</a><br><br>And come join the Aestas Book Blog <a href="http://www.facebook.com/pages/Aestas-Book-Blog/332404836826905" rel="nofollow noopener"> Facebook Page</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="3687145281925084750" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_377268675" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/377268675" />
    <a title="Kat Kennedy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3270188-kat-kennedy"><img alt="Kat Kennedy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1537750381p2/3270188.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/377268675?book_show_action=true">Jul 26, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kat Kennedy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kat Kennedy" href="/user/show/3270188-kat-kennedy">Kat Kennedy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3270188-kat-kennedy?shelf=to-ya-or-not-to-ya">to-ya-or-not-to-ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3270188-kat-kennedy?shelf=contemporary-fiction">contemporary-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3270188-kat-kennedy?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3270188-kat-kennedy?shelf=kat-s-book-reviews">kat-s-book-reviews</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3270188-kat-kennedy?shelf=leaves-awesomeness-behind">leaves-awesomeness-behind</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer377268675" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10258001952772495851">When try­ing to find a way to describe this book – I set­tled on this: Push­ing The Lim­its is the clos­est I’ve ever got­ten to read­ing a Machetta book.<br/><br/>For any­one famil­iar with me or Machetta – that is the high­est praise I give.<br/><br/>Very rarely does a book make me laugh and cry at all – let alone mul­ti­ple times. But that’s what this book did. And really, what the hell kind of badass reviewer am I when I’m brought to snivel­ing, snotty tears by a book? <br/><br/>Noah and Echo don’t talk at school. Noah i</span>
  <span id="freeText10258001952772495851" style="display:none">When try­ing to find a way to describe this book – I set­tled on this: Push­ing The Lim­its is the clos­est I’ve ever got­ten to read­ing a Machetta book.<br /><br />For any­one famil­iar with me or Machetta – that is the high­est praise I give.<br /><br />Very rarely does a book make me laugh and cry at all – let alone mul­ti­ple times. But that’s what this book did. And really, what the hell kind of badass reviewer am I when I’m brought to snivel­ing, snotty tears by a book? <br /><br />Noah and Echo don’t talk at school. Noah is the atyp­i­cal bad boy and Echo is the for­mer Teen Queen on the verge of reclaim­ing her for­mer glory. But Noah and Echo have a lot more in com­mon than they real­ize. They’re both bro­ken. This book is told through both of their view points as they start ther­apy and their lives start to unravel and they get pushed closer and closer together by their circumstances.<br /><br />What I love is that there are three real­i­ties in this book. McGarry takes into account that there is Noah’s truth, Echo’s truth and then there’s this whole other crea­ture we’ll call What Is Actu­ally Hap­pen­ing. I haven’t seen some­one show flawed nar­ra­tion this well in a long time. What McGarry cap­tured per­fectly is that dis­con­nect while keep­ing me plugged in an sympathetic.<br /><br />Exam­ple.<br /><br />Noah is fight­ing for cus­tody of his younger broth­ers. When his par­ents died, he and his sib­lings were sep­a­rated. Noah was placed in a series of very bad and neg­li­gent homes while his broth­ers were placed with a cus­tody fam­ily who restrict his access to his sib­lings and are try­ing to adopt them.<br /><br />Echo’s father and his new wife (Echo’s old babysit­ter) have a very rocky, unhealthy rela­tion­ship. He is con­trol­ling, the new wife is preg­nant and Echo is des­per­ate to try and make con­tact with her mother (who has been cut off from con­tact by Echo’s father).<br /><br />At least – that is how it looks at the begin­ning. And it’s very easy to think that these adults in Echo and Noah’s lives are hor­ri­ble. But whilst Echo and Noah con­tinue to see them that way for awhile, and whilst I as the reader remained com­pletely empa­thetic as to why Noah and Echo saw them that way, it becomes clear that the sit­u­a­tion is not as cut and dry as that.<br /><br />By the cli­max of both Echo and Noah’s sto­ries I was weep­ing uncon­trol­lably. I still cry when I think about those two parts of the book. McGarry’s writ­ing is pow­er­ful, emo­tive. Her char­ac­ter voices for both Noah and Echo were very well done – reflect­ing on their dis­tinct per­son­al­i­ties and char­ac­ter­is­tics. The plot con­tained lit­tle action and was largely car­ried by the myr­iad of rela­tion­ships and the mys­tery of Echo’s past – so fans of more fast paced, active nov­els may want to steer clear.<br /><br />Mrs Collins, their ther­a­pist, plays an almost omnipo­tent, god­like char­ac­ter in the novel and brought a fresh, lov­able addi­tion. She was one of my favourites.<br /><br />Over all, I think most read­ers are going to love this one. One of the absolute best books of 2012!</span>
  <a data-text-id="10258001952772495851" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_331167722" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/331167722" />
    <a title="Giselle" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4800103-giselle"><img alt="Giselle" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1310159877p2/4800103.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/331167722?book_show_action=true">May 16, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Giselle" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Giselle" href="/user/show/4800103-giselle">Giselle</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4800103-giselle?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4800103-giselle?shelf=ebook">ebook</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer331167722" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6668457302896966222">It's no secret that this book has been getting insane reviews. Being the persistent black sheep that I am, I was incredibly wary of the hype it was garnering, certain that it would fail to impress me. Oh boy. Oh <i>freaking</i> boy!! Was I ever wrong. I loved this so hard! <br/><br/>Echo and Noah… Echo. Noah. Nocho?<br/><br/>Echo has been through an extremely distressing, life altering ordeal because of which she's suffering post-traumatic stress, with the worst side effect being memory loss. She doesn't remember what hap</span>
  <span id="freeText6668457302896966222" style="display:none">It's no secret that this book has been getting insane reviews. Being the persistent black sheep that I am, I was incredibly wary of the hype it was garnering, certain that it would fail to impress me. Oh boy. Oh <i>freaking</i> boy!! Was I ever wrong. I loved this so hard! <br><br>Echo and Noah… Echo. Noah. Nocho?<br><br>Echo has been through an extremely distressing, life altering ordeal because of which she's suffering post-traumatic stress, with the worst side effect being memory loss. She doesn't remember what happened. All she has are the scars. From popular to outsider, Echo's troubled state-of-mind is harsh and unstable. One of the best character development I've read, she made me a part of her. With only the span of a few pages, she had me immersed in her world, in her heart and soul. Every layer of her being is gradually being laid out for us to become equally mesmerized and perplexed by. Her scars, her babysitter-turned-stepmother, her dead brother, along with her PTSD, she has the world on her shoulders and I was right there alongside her, sharing the weight. <br><br>With an equally burdened soul, Noah only wants two things: Jacob, and Tyler. After his parents died in a fire, the three brothers have been in the foster system and Noah wants nothing more than his family back together. The emotions in his perspective begin from our very first glance into his melancholy life. His relationship with his brothers brought tears to my eyes, pulling me in wholeheartedly. He may be tortured and angry - the perfect bad boy image -, yet, underneath his tough exterior he's a loving, caring person who would move heaven and earth for those boys, and, eventually, for Echo. This is a wonderful example of a perfectly woven dual perspective. Both characters are highly vivid, evoking powerful emotions that truly connect the reader to each character. Sketching them one page at a time. <br><br>Romantic. Passionate. Frustrating. Filled to the brink with chemistry. The love story in Pushing the Limits is <i>raw</i>. This is true love at its purest form, with sacrifices and compromises, incredible obstacles, and learning to trust without holding back. Like true love, it's not easy, and it's not always painless. We're dealing with two damaged individuals who need to find themselves before they let themselves find each other. Covering a lot more ground than the love story itself, we get intense, emotional ups and downs that just about gave me heart palpitations. While reading, I quickly lost myself in this incredibly enchanting story, experiencing a multitude of complex emotions. By the time I put this book down, I had a heavy heart and a set smile. <br><br>Combining love and loss, friendship and family, the unfairnesses of life and the determination to overcome them, Pushing the Limits is a book that is not only to be read, but cherished. This is one gem that shines!<br><br>--<br>For more of my reviews, visit my blog at <a href="http://www.xpressoreads.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Xpresso Reads</a> <a href="http://www.xpressoreads.com/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380358334i/709537.png" width="380" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="6668457302896966222" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_383743905" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/383743905" />
    <a title="Reynje" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5590906-reynje"><img alt="Reynje" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1473722441p2/5590906.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/383743905?book_show_action=true">Aug 04, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Reynje" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Reynje" href="/user/show/5590906-reynje">Reynje</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer383743905" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11751015016267025217"><b>2.5 stars</b><br/><br/>Part way through Pushing The Limits, I put down my kindle and thought: <i>Am I (gasp) too <s>old</s> crotchety and cynical for this?</i> I wanted to like this book, but ultimately I just ended up feeling like I’d been caught in a stampede of drama llamas. <br/><br/>Contemporary YA is probably my favourite genre. And I like books that challenge me emotionally. But while I had no real problem with Noah and Echo’s respective Issues-with-a-capital”I”, something about this just felt off to me. It didn’t feel sincer</span>
  <span id="freeText11751015016267025217" style="display:none"><b>2.5 stars</b><br /><br />Part way through Pushing The Limits, I put down my kindle and thought: <i>Am I (gasp) too <s>old</s> crotchety and cynical for this?</i> I wanted to like this book, but ultimately I just ended up feeling like I’d been caught in a stampede of drama llamas. <br /><br />Contemporary YA is probably my favourite genre. And I like books that challenge me emotionally. But while I had no real problem with Noah and Echo’s respective Issues-with-a-capital”I”, something about this just felt off to me. It didn’t feel sincere, and therefore it didn’t resonate with me. <br /><br />Don’t get me wrong – McGarry’s characters have valid, realistic obstacles and conflicts to contend with. It was just something about the execution that didn’t work for me. It felt too overwrought, too obvious, too overwhelmingly angsty for me to really engage with the story. The treatment of several of the (abundant) issues fell flat for me – it read more like an grab for an emotional reaction than a really nuanced discussion of serious topics like mental illness and abuse. <br /><br />On a scale of Elkeles (Chain Reaction) to Echols (Going Too Far), Pushing The Limits falls somewhere in the middle for me. There’s probably a time when I would have adored this book, and I can honestly see why others love it, but it was a problematic book for me on a few levels. The lack of subtlety for one (which is probably just a personal taste thing), and the reliance on over-used clichés for another. I feel like I’ve met all of these characters before, I’ve heard the same bad-boy meets former popular girl angst too many times before. <br /><br />(Also, Noah’s repeated use of expressions like “siren”, “nymph” and “seductress” produced more snort-laughs than swoons from me. For example:<i>"A ghost of that siren smile graced her lips as she tilted her head closer to mine, creating the undeniable pull of the sailor lost at sea to the beautiful goddess calling him home."</i> If that quote just made you melt, go read this book immediately. However if, like me, you just stifled a pterodactyl-like screech of hysteria, this book might not really set your loins on fire. )<br /><br />Definitely recommended for fans of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/4268157.Perfect_Chemistry__Perfect_Chemistry___1_" title="Perfect Chemistry (Perfect Chemistry, #1) by Simone Elkeles" rel="nofollow noopener">Perfect Chemistry</a>. Just not really my thing, unfortunately. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="11751015016267025217" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer9644685253065302329"><b>5 Stars!</b><br/><br/><i>**RE-READ on Audible! Loved it just as much the second time around!</i><br/><br/><a href='http://s1279.photobucket.com/user/Christyb23/media/Book%20Reviews%205/b4e8f075-903f-42da-a5eb-1fd54b0d693b_zps994778ea.jpg.html' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>

She has been through so much heartache. It has destroyed a lot of things impo</span>
  <span id="freeText9644685253065302329" style="display:none"><b>5 Stars!</b><br><br><i>**RE-READ on Audible! Loved it just as much the second time around!</i><br><br><a href="http://s1279.photobucket.com/user/Christyb23/media/Book%20Reviews%205/b4e8f075-903f-42da-a5eb-1fd54b0d693b_zps994778ea.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1411894575i/11296654.jpg" alt=" photo b4e8f075-903f-42da-a5eb-1fd54b0d693b_zps994778ea.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>This was not your normal romance story... In fact, normal is one of the last words you would use to describe Noah, Echo or their relationship. Echo was such a strong character. She has been through so much heartache. Not only has she lost her brother Aires, the one person who she felt loved her unconditionally, but she has had a major trauma that she has not even fully discovered. It has destroyed a lot of things important to her; her reputation, friends, art etc. Noah hasn't had it easy either. After losing both parents in a fire, he is in foster care separated from his two little brothers. He may be a sexy, tough, bad boy but there is a side of him that you will fall for! He is loving, loyal, and obviously a family centered guy. I adored him! Noah and Echo though both damaged, develop a beautiful but difficult relationship. <br><br><i>
  <blockquote> Her eyes met mine again. "So what does this mean for us?" I lowered my forehead to hers "it means your mine." </blockquote>
</i><br>Seriously loved Noah!<br><br>Echo and Noah's journey was full of heartache, healing, and most importantly acceptance. Their counselor Mrs Collins was great. She truly cared about the both of them and went above and beyond to help them. I have to say I really hated Echo's mom <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ not just for the terrible thing she did to Echo- though that was part of it, but her attitude when Echo finally got to confront her. She didn't even want to see her really or apologize? That woman was bat shit crazy!  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> her dad could be selfish at times, and very controlling, but I think he really did love Echo and want what was best for her. Now the whole Ashley situation was something else... Another character I lothed was Grace. What. A. Bitch! Just saying... Worst friend ever! Lila on the other hand was a wonderful best friend. She was supportive of Echo and didn't turn her back on her. I also loved Isaiah, him fixing Aires car was great and he was like family to Noah. Beth I didn't care for at first but she really grew on me! I especially loved the relationship between Noah and his brothers. I couldn't get through a scene with those three without crying. It was bittersweet what happens with them at the end but I think Noah realized it worked out for the best. <br><br>There were many points in this book I ended up in tears. I couldn't help myself. The story touched me. It also had funny parts too. I wanted to savor this book and make it last, but that seemed impossible because I couldn't put it down! It was a truly beautiful story of pain, love, heartache, discovery, understanding and acceptance. If you haven't read this book you are missing out!!!<br><br><a href="http://s1279.photobucket.com/user/Christyb23/media/Book%20Reviews%205/d4b05bf9-e79e-4e8c-8ed6-4e6ebc4b5a4a_zps8c518acc.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">

</a></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

<div id="review_258594832" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/258594832" />
    <a title="♥Rachel♥" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5481477-rachel"><img alt="♥Rachel♥" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1363996055p2/5481477.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/258594832?book_show_action=true">Jan 08, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="♥Rachel♥" class="user" itemprop="url" name="♥Rachel♥" href="/user/show/5481477-rachel">♥Rachel♥</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5481477-rachel?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5481477-rachel?shelf=netgalley-e-book">netgalley-e-book</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5481477-rachel?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer258594832" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1732672855559983601"><br/>I <b>
  <i>ADORED</i>
</b> this story! <br/><br/>Seventeen year-old Echo Emerson used to be part of the popular crowd. Two years ago things changed. Her parents divorced, her babysitter became her step-mother, and her older brother Aires died in combat. But this is not the event that changed everything for Echo. Two years ago, an event she can't remember resulted in her waking up in the hospital two-days later, with injuries up and down both her arms. Injuries that left her with ugly scars, and a restraining order in p</span>
  <span id="freeText1732672855559983601" style="display:none"><br />I <b>
  <i>ADORED</i>
</b> this story! <br /><br />Seventeen year-old Echo Emerson used to be part of the popular crowd. Two years ago things changed. Her parents divorced, her babysitter became her step-mother, and her older brother Aires died in combat. But this is not the event that changed everything for Echo. Two years ago, an event she can't remember resulted in her waking up in the hospital two-days later, with injuries up and down both her arms. Injuries that left her with ugly scars, and a restraining order in place against her mother. Because of the "event" Echo has been mandated by the State to attend therapy sessions. She has just been assigned a new therapist, one that she shares with Noah Hutchins, resident bad-boy with a reputation of one-night-stands. <br /><br />Noah Hutchins has his own set of problems. Two and half years ago, he was on the honor-roll, competed in sports, and had the perfect family. Two loving parents and two-younger brothers. This was before his parents were killed in a house fire. Now Noah is separated from his little brothers. He's in one foster home, while they are in another. Noah's dream is to get his brothers back and reunite what's left of his family. He's had a string of bad luck with the homes he's been placed in. This is why he is now in court mandated therapy sessions, and on limited visitation with his younger brothers. <br /><br />Echo and Noah's worlds collide when Echo is assigned to tutor Noah. These two don't immediately hit it off. At first they really don't care for each other but a common goal presents itself, and they unite. Noah and Echo didn't realize they had so much in common. What follows, is a common bond over their tragedies and a growing attraction! I was just <i>gaga</i> over this romance! There is heat and tension but also understanding and empathy. Noah and Echo start to truly care for one another. There were so many scenes of <i>swoon</i>! Weak-in-the-knees swoon! You know me, I have to share a little of at least one! Here you go: <br /><br /><b>
  <i>* "Keep it up Echo. I'm all about foreplay." She laughed so loudly, she slapped a hand over her mouth, yet the giggles escaped. "You are so full of yourself. You think because girls swoon over you and let you into their pants on the first try that I'll follow suit. Think again. Besides, I have your number now. Every time you try to look all dark and dangerous, I'll picture you wearing a pink striped polo, collar up, and a pair of pleated chinos." No way. I stalked over to Echo, feeling like a tiger after its prey. She backed up against the wall, but I kept up my approach. I pressed against her, feeling each sensual curve. I wanted to touch every inch of her body. Her sweet smell intoxicated me. Her eyes kept her laughter, but her smile faded as she bit her lower lip. Damn, did she have any idea what she was doing? For a girl hell-bent on keeping me away, she sure did everything to turn me on. </i>
</b><br /><br />There is a mystery behind Echo's injuries that is gradually revealed to her. What we find out is so heartbreaking and INFURIATING at the same time. <b>BE WARNED</b>, you are going to HATE Echo's parents and the self-centered step-mother, Ashley!! The father constantly put Ashley before Echo, even when she desperately needed him! I was overjoyed when Echo started standing up to her father and told him things he needed to hear! Don't even get me started on the mother. Still, I think the parents got off way too easy in my opinion! Trust me, you are going to shake a fist or two while reading this story because of them! Ms. McGarry did an excellent job writing these awful people. <br /><br />Noah and his little brothers touched my heart! What they lost and its consequences was heart-wrenching. Noah <i>loves</i> his brothers. He yearns to give them the security his family once had. This is so difficult for someone his age. You can't help but empathize with his feelings of helplessness. <br /><br />I must congratulate Katie McGarry on her wonderful ability to make me care so much for these characters. It's so important to me that I connect with the main characters in a story, and she really made that happen. I highly recommend this story! I thought it was an amazing debut for Ms. McGarry, and I'll be reading anything else she decides to write! <br /><br /><b>*</b><i>Quote is taken from uncorrected ARC. </i><br /><br /><i>Thank you to Netgalley and Harlequin Teen for allowing me to read this amazing story!</i> </span>
  <a data-text-id="1732672855559983601" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer8486860044893718663">Spoiler Free Review<br/>5 STARS out of 5<br/>Genre: YA-Mature Contemporary Romance<br/><br/><b> THIS IS .31CENTS on Amazon U.S. 5-5-14 If you have not read this book I HIGHLY RECOMMEND IT!</b> buy link: <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://amzn.com/B00B0A5Y78'>http://amzn.com/B00B0A5Y78</a><br/><br/><i>Pushing the Limits was an appropriate name for this book and if i could sum up my feelings in one word it would be <u>BREAKTHROUGH</u>.
