  <span id="freeText8486860044893718663" style="display:none">Spoiler Free Review<br />5 STARS out of 5<br />Genre: YA-Mature Contemporary Romance<br /><br /><b> THIS IS .31CENTS on Amazon U.S. 5-5-14 If you have not read this book I HIGHLY RECOMMEND IT!</b> buy link: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://amzn.com/B00B0A5Y78">http://amzn.com/B00B0A5Y78</a><br /><br /><i>Pushing the Limits was an appropriate name for this book and if i could sum up my feelings in one word it would be <u>BREAKTHROUGH</u>. Which is what i waited for the whole book. A breakthrough the act of finally overcoming or reaching an achievement by penetrating a wall/enemy that is restricting you from getting any progress. That wall...that enemy is what Echo and Noah faced on a daily bases.</i><br /><br />Echo's wall was her memory<br />Noah's enemy was the system<br /><br /><b>"So Echo's sophomore year, she's the star of the school, right? She's on the dance team, advanced classes, honor roll, art guru, Miss popularity, and she's got Luke Manning feeling her up between classes. One month before school lets out- she disappears."</b> Beth's eyes widened and she spread her fingers out like a magician doing a trick. This was not where i thought this story would go. Isaiah watched my reaction and nodded. <b>"Poof."</b><br /><b>"Gone,"</b> added Beth<br /><b>"Vanished,"</b> -Isaiah<br /><b>"Lost."</b> -Beth<br /><b>"Evaporated.</b> -Isaiah<br /><b>"Gone,"</b> repeated Beth<br /><br />Echo Emerson is now the shell of her old self. After her sudden absence at the end of her sophomore year Echo was never the same. Of course the rumor mill takes over and becomes out of control by the time she starts Junior year. However the truth is only known by a few. And unfortunately Echo is not one of them. Her memory of what happened to alter her life and leave her arms badly scarred is suppressed. Bummer right? The doctors all say it will come back when she is ready to handle it. Now Echo is forced to see her school shrink Mrs. Collins. <br />Things change for Echo after she cross paths with Noah Hutchins. Noah is the school loner who has a rep for one night stands and getting high off weed. After butting heads the two realize they share a common need. And that is to read their case files for information. Information they both are not allowed to have yet crave more than their next breath. Of course they soon start to crave each other as well.<br /><br />Reading about these two made me feel like i was coming in to contact with static electricity. Check it out<br /><i>'She pushed off her toes toward me, guiding my head down, and gently kissed my lips. No. This wouldn't be goodbye. I'd fill her up and make her realize she'd always be empty without me.'</i> -Noah's inner monologue <br /><b>They also connected on a deeper level. Check this out</b><br /><i>'Her shoulders never shook. No tears streamed down her face. The worst type of crying wasn't the kind everyone could see-the wailing on the street corners, the tearing at clothes. No the worst kind happened when your soul wept and no matter what you did, there was no way to comfort it. A section withered and became a scar on the part of your soul that survived. For people like me and Echo, our souls contained more scar tissue than life.'</i> - Noah's inner monologue<br /><br />Seriously.. Read this book! <br /><br /><u>Fave lines</u><br /><b>"Stop sulking already. If you would have screwed her when you first met her, like i told you to, you wouldn't be twisted like a damn pretzel."</b> -Beth<br /><br /><b>"I'll always save you." Because i would. I'd move heaven and earth. I'd willingly walk into hell and stay there. I'd give up anything and everything for him.</b> -Noah<br /><br /><b>"Come here, baby." And with my words, Echo leaned into me: soft, pliant, broken. "You're not alone." I whispered into her hair as i cradled her in my arms. "You're not alone because you have me."</b><br /> -Noah<br /><br /><u>Thoughts</u><br />This book is unputdownable! I loved it! The writing is superb and the characters are captivating. You instantly fall in love with Echo and Noah and their friends. I cannot wait for Beth's book. If you have not read this book READ IT!<br /><b>Echo-</b> Is kind, hardworking and loving. I enjoyed watching her come out her shell and face her peers head on. She was stronger than she even realized. But when she did it was AMAZING. I hated how she allowed herself to be treated unfair by that BITCH Grace. And I hate the social class placed on kids in school and i hate hate hate followers. I loved her and Noah's relationship how they connected and shared their fears, struggles and goals with each other. I hope to get glimpses of her and Noah together in Beth's book.<br /><b>Noah-</b> What is their not to love about him. His strength and his love was so beautiful. It made him even more sexier if thats possible. He took no crap what so ever when it came to his friends and family. The guy exudes AWESOMENESS! He was also FEARLESS he had no qualms with taking on the system and fighting for what he believed. He also possessed GRACE when it came to accepting what he knew in his heart was right.<br /><b>Lila-</b> I liked Lila she proved to be a good friend. True she had her moments. But she never turned her back on Echo unlike some...<br /><b>Mrs. Collins</b> I loved her. I love how she really cared for both Echo and Noah. She championed for them and never let them down not once. <br /><b>Beth-</b> Was a whole sloppy mess but in a good way. I cannot wait for her story.<br /><br />My Ratings<br />Characters- Lovable, Charming and Witty<br />Writing Style- Solid and Genuine <br />Plot/Storyline- Excellent<br />Steam Factor- Medium/Moderately Steamy<br />Overall- I LOVED IT! READ IT!!!</span>

<div id="review_1293729704" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1293729704" />
    <a title="Pearl Angeli" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/31514572-pearl-angeli"><img alt="Pearl Angeli" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1588420465p2/31514572.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1293729704?book_show_action=true">May 30, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Pearl Angeli" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Pearl Angeli" href="/user/show/31514572-pearl-angeli">Pearl Angeli</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780373210862" href="/book/show/16145531-pushing-the-limits">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31514572-pearl-angeli?shelf=2015-reads">2015-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31514572-pearl-angeli?shelf=young-adult-contemporary">young-adult-contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31514572-pearl-angeli?shelf=owned-physical-copy">owned-physical-copy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31514572-pearl-angeli?shelf=damn-this-guy-is-perfect">damn-this-guy-is-perfect</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1293729704" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6877579491740134210">I enjoyed <b>Pushing the Limits</b> so much! It is such a sweet and emotional book. Actually my kind of book. I love troubled (but not angsty and annoying) main characters because it challenges me to dig deeper into their past and understand why they become what they are. <br/><br/>The story centers on <b>Noah Hutchins</b>-- a guy who became an orphan at a very early age because of the accident that happened to his family several years ago, and <b>Echo Emerson</b>-- a girl who suffers a memory suppression because of the freak</span>
  <span id="freeText6877579491740134210" style="display:none">I enjoyed <b>Pushing the Limits</b> so much! It is such a sweet and emotional book. Actually my kind of book. I love troubled (but not angsty and annoying) main characters because it challenges me to dig deeper into their past and understand why they become what they are. <br /><br />The story centers on <b>Noah Hutchins</b>-- a guy who became an orphan at a very early age because of the accident that happened to his family several years ago, and <b>Echo Emerson</b>-- a girl who suffers a memory suppression because of the freaky incident that happened to her and her mom. Both of them share a couple of subjects together at school but they never had a chance to be good friends until their new clinical social worker <b>Mrs. Collins</b> came and partnered them for tutoring sessions.<br /><br />This book was full of emotions, but that wasn't the only thing that made me feel compelled to the book. It had a very entertaining start. There was humor and the characters instantly clicked the first time they collided. The chemistry was so good I can't help but sigh. I love <b>Noah</b>m he's a perfect book boyfriend. I love the way he's protective towards her brothers and towards <b>Echo</b>. <br /><br /><b>Echo</b> is also one adorable character. Although she's vulnerable at the start, I admired her character development-- how she became tough in dealing her dilemmas. The secondary characters are also adorable. <b>Isaiah</b> is so cute and although I don't kind of connect with <b>Beth</b> at the start, my feelings toward her changed at the last chapters of the book. And of course, I love <b>Mrs. Collins</b>. She's cool! Every guidance counselor should be like her!<br /><br />I just love this book! The only thing that kept me from rating it a perfect 5 was the <i>
  <b>romance</b>
</i> . I love Noah and Echo's chemistry and their sizzling, make-out scenes but I was looking for more. The family drama was heavily emphasized in this book and I wish the author also made a great highlight in the romance because omg, they are perfect for each other. <b>I want more Noah and Echo moments!!!</b><br /><br />But as a whole, it's a great and unforgettable read. It's my first <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/4575371.Katie_McGarry" title="Katie McGarry" rel="nofollow noopener">Katie McGarry</a> book and I'm impressed with her writing style. I'll definitely read more of her books!<br /><br />Rating: 4 Stars<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="6877579491740134210" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

              <span id="reviewTextContainer2308152116" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer10472633309376308737">My first Katie McGarry read and was beyond pleased! I am a sucker for YA, and although the main characters are only eighteen, they spoke and acted more mature for their age.<br/><br/>This had a unique storyline, there was intelligible conversation and was emotionally charged!<br/><br/>Noah and Echo are seniors in high school and both dealing with horrific pasts. Noah would rather forget the event which led to his now screwed up life and wanting nothing more than to be reunited with his brothers. Echo wishes she cou</span>
  <span id="freeText10472633309376308737" style="display:none">My first Katie McGarry read and was beyond pleased! I am a sucker for YA, and although the main characters are only eighteen, they spoke and acted more mature for their age.<br /><br />This had a unique storyline, there was intelligible conversation and was emotionally charged!<br /><br />Noah and Echo are seniors in high school and both dealing with horrific pasts. Noah would rather forget the event which led to his now screwed up life and wanting nothing more than to be reunited with his brothers. Echo wishes she could remember the event which tore her world to shreds and left endless nightmares in it's wake.<br /><br />Noah is known as a “stoner” by other classmates and his only relationships are one night stands. Echo is a straight A student and only wants to be normal again so she can be in a relationship.<br /><br /> <i>Are you going to take me to the Valentine’s Dance? Am I going to be more than another girl in the backseat of your car or will I be a joke between you and your friends?”</i><br /><br /> <i><b>I don’t know.</b> The truth stuck in my throat. I wanted to tell her she’d be more, but I couldn’t. I didn’t do attachments and here was this amazing creature, asking me for one.</i><br /><br />Noah is a ward of the nightmarish system called Foster Care, and Echo’s family home unit is slowly sucking the life out of her.<br /><br /> <i>”I want normal, Noah. Can you give me normal?”</i><br /><br /> <i>”When are you going to figure out that doesn’t exist for people like us?” ..... She could pretend, but she’d never return to the girl without scars.</i><br /><br />Their social worker, Mrs. Collins, is “hell on wheels” funny, but because of her tenacity and genuine care for Noah and Echo, she is pivotal in getting their lives pointed in the right direction and unwittingly into each other’s arms :)<br /><br />I totally enjoyed watching Noah and Echo’s relationship evolve from mutual irritation and distrust for one another bloom into the sweetest love.<br /><br />I am anxious to read more by this author!!</span>

<div id="review_332327131" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/332327131" />
    <a title="Kristin (KC) - Traveling Sister" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4971692-kristin-kc---traveling-sister"><img alt="Kristin (KC) - Traveling Sister" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1486056026p2/4971692.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/332327131?book_show_action=true">May 18, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kristin (KC) - Traveling Sister" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kristin (KC) - Traveling Sister" href="/user/show/4971692-kristin-kc---traveling-sister">Kristin (KC) - Traveling Sister</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4971692-kristin-kc---traveling-sister?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer332327131" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5274089390086621449"><i>Pushing the Limits</i> thoroughly pushed me to mine from its gut-wrenching start to its emotional finish. I devoured every drop of this amazing story as it brought me to hell and back right along with it. Every element I long for in a book was generously provided; engaging writing, broken yet lovable characters, sexual tension, angst and heartache, and finally, growth and sweet redemption. <br/><br/>Echo has survived a heartbreaking tragedy that has left her with extreme physical and emotional scars, but the </span>
  <span id="freeText5274089390086621449" style="display:none"><i>Pushing the Limits</i> thoroughly pushed me to mine from its gut-wrenching start to its emotional finish. I devoured every drop of this amazing story as it brought me to hell and back right along with it. Every element I long for in a book was generously provided; engaging writing, broken yet lovable characters, sexual tension, angst and heartache, and finally, growth and sweet redemption. <br><br>Echo has survived a heartbreaking tragedy that has left her with extreme physical and emotional scars, but the severe trauma of the event has taken away her memory of that fateful day. When her school counselor provides her with a tutoring job, Echo comes face-to-face with Noah...a fellow classmate who suffers torment of his own and sees Echo as some privileged, spoiled rich girl living the good life. However, these two lost souls slowly learn that they have more in common than they could ever imagine, and together, they face their demons in a fight for a chance at 'normalcy'. <br><br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>The worst type of crying wasn't the kind everyone could see--the wailing on the street corners, the tearing at clothes. No, the worst kind happened when your soul wept and no matter what you did, there was no way to comfort it. A section withered and became a scar on the part of your soul that survived...For people like me and Echo, our souls contained more scars than life.</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br>I felt the unfair way Echo's peers reacted towards her 'defect' was, for the most part, sadly yet realistically portrayed. Echo was initially a pushover who easily conformed to what others expected of her--but I understood her need for love and acceptance as she falsely believed that allowing others to take the reins over her broken life would temporarily make things easier.  Her eventual 'I'm worthy' epiphany pretty much had me throwing fists in the air!<br><br>This story was so wonderfully constructed and the author did an amazing job in bringing Echo's mental struggle to life. I was captivated and completely sucked right into her internal breakdown to the point where I actually felt myself struggling for air at times. The alternating perspectives between Echo and Noah  flowed flawlessly and allowed for an in-depth understanding of both characters. Noah's pain and strife reduced me to tears, as did his eventual happiness. As tragic as this story seemed, it was honestly an eye-opening, touching journey to an imperfect, but utterly heartwarming resolve.<b> Simply beautiful! </b><br><br><a href="http://tinypic.com?ref=2mh7uop" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img height="50" width="50" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380347313i/701667.jpg" alt="Image and video hosting by TinyPic" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><b>
  <u>Book Stats:</u>

A heartbreaking journey of two emotionally damaged teens finding strength in one another.<br><b>▪ Writing:</b> Expressive, engaging, and intense. <br><b>▪ POV:</b> 1st Person: Dual Perspectives. <br><b>▪	 Cliffhanger:</b> None<br><b>▪	 Next Installment:</b> Character Spinoff<br><br><a href="http://prettywordsbookblog.com" rel="nofollow noopener">

<div id="review_229397454" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/229397454" />
    <a title="Kelly" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1816678-kelly"><img alt="Kelly" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442507719p2/1816678.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/229397454?book_show_action=true">Oct 31, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kelly" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kelly" href="/user/show/1816678-kelly">Kelly</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer229397454" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9482495518398615911">I can think of only three books that have ever made me cry, one of which is Pushing the Limits by Katie McGarry. If you haven’t gotten this one on pre-order yet, go ye forth and do so. This is a 2012 must read. <br/><br/>Since I write paranormal, I don’t often get a chance to pick up YA contemporary. But obviously I’m missing out. Especially if the other titles out there right now are half as engrossing as Katie McGarry’s debut. <br/><br/>After finishing this novel, I wanted to start it again. Because I missed the </span>
  <span id="freeText9482495518398615911" style="display:none">I can think of only three books that have ever made me cry, one of which is Pushing the Limits by Katie McGarry. If you haven’t gotten this one on pre-order yet, go ye forth and do so. This is a 2012 must read. <br /><br />Since I write paranormal, I don’t often get a chance to pick up YA contemporary. But obviously I’m missing out. Especially if the other titles out there right now are half as engrossing as Katie McGarry’s debut. <br /><br />After finishing this novel, I wanted to start it again. Because I missed the characters. They were THAT real to me. The relationships in this book are so tangible and heartrending and gut wrenchingly spot on.<br /><br />There are several threads running through this book at once, which is just one of the reasons that I loved this story so much. It’s told from alternating points of view. So our two main characters, Echo and Noah, begin with their own agendas in mind, their own separate problems and struggles. Then, against their wills, they are brought together by their circumstances. <br />As the story progresses, the lives of these two young people (and consequently their struggles) begin to intertwine. They become enmeshed with one another and I became enmeshed with them, snared by the aestheticism of their voices and their world and their all-too-real dilemmas. <br /><br />And I haven’t even gotten to the romance in this novel, which is one of the major themes. <br /><br />Echo and Noah = HELLO CHEMISTRY.<br /><br />The sexual tension between the two is just about unbearable—and that’s delicious when that happens in a novel, isn’t it? Sweet torture is what I’ll call it. <br /><br />More than the tension, though, there is also a gradual build to the relationship between them. And I’m a sucker for a romance that is layered by one moment or encounter at a time, and then another. <br />I know I started this review by saying that this novel made me cry, but it also made me laugh. A lot. Ms. McGarry had a true gift for voice, and many of Echo’s internal moments sent me over the edge with giggles. At one point, I had to put the book down because I was laughing so hard. And as for Noah, I can say that the male voice feels startlingly accurate--I think I gained many insights to the male brain! <br /><br />So I have a “favorites” shelf in my house. And this one has a special place there, because I’m going to be reading it again, and then again. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="9482495518398615911" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/621433739" />
    <a title="Heather K (dentist in my spare time)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13070326-heather-k-dentist-in-my-spare-time"><img alt="Heather K (dentist in my spare time)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1365526640p2/13070326.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/621433739?book_show_action=true">May 21, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Heather K (dentist in my spare time)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Heather K (dentist in my spare time)" href="/user/show/13070326-heather-k-dentist-in-my-spare-time">Heather K (dentist in my spare time)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/15534922-pushing-the-limits">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13070326-heather-k-dentist-in-my-spare-time?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13070326-heather-k-dentist-in-my-spare-time?shelf=hype-hype-hype">hype-hype-hype</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13070326-heather-k-dentist-in-my-spare-time?shelf=m-f">m-f</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13070326-heather-k-dentist-in-my-spare-time?shelf=loved-it">loved-it</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13070326-heather-k-dentist-in-my-spare-time?shelf=addiction-or-mental-disorders">addiction-or-mental-disorders</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13070326-heather-k-dentist-in-my-spare-time?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13070326-heather-k-dentist-in-my-spare-time?shelf=little-to-no-sex-content">little-to-no-sex-content</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13070326-heather-k-dentist-in-my-spare-time?shelf=full-of-angst">full-of-angst</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13070326-heather-k-dentist-in-my-spare-time?shelf=made-me-cry">made-me-cry</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13070326-heather-k-dentist-in-my-spare-time?shelf=net-galley">net-galley</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer621433739" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6690662511565180940"><b>**Only $0.31 at Amazon US, 5/5/14- YES, 31 CENTS!**</b><br/><br/>**4.5 stars**<br/><br/><b>Wonderful, guilty-pleasure, angsty teen goodness!!</b> <br/><br/>When it comes to rating these hurt-comfort teen stories I tend to just go with my gut and let reason fly out the window. Sure, this book has its fair share of issues. Everything is wrapped up perfectly and neatly, everyone gets over their issues in a timely fashion, and the bad boy is tamed by love. However, did I love it? <i>You bet your butt I did!!</i> <br/><br/>I have a weakness for big brothers</span>
  <span id="freeText6690662511565180940" style="display:none"><b>**Only $0.31 at Amazon US, 5/5/14- YES, 31 CENTS!**</b><br /><br />**4.5 stars**<br /><br /><b>Wonderful, guilty-pleasure, angsty teen goodness!!</b> <br /><br />When it comes to rating these hurt-comfort teen stories I tend to just go with my gut and let reason fly out the window. Sure, this book has its fair share of issues. Everything is wrapped up perfectly and neatly, everyone gets over their issues in a timely fashion, and the bad boy is tamed by love. However, did I love it? <i>You bet your butt I did!!</i> <br /><br />I have a weakness for big brothers caring for younger siblings after the death of a parent (see <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10401084.Storm__Elemental___1_" title="Storm (Elemental, #1) by Brigid Kemmerer" rel="nofollow noopener">Storm</a>). What can I say, I love a strong man who puts his siblings ahead of himself. Noah was a character I could get behind. And I liked the way his relationship progressed with Echo. It felt nicely paced to me and not insta-love-ish. I appreciated the talented writing and the restraint of Katie McGarry. I dug them together. <br /><br />I think that the story that captivated me the most was Noah's, actually. I enjoyed his voice the best. I felt like when the writer was talking as Echo, my feelings were being more manipulated, if that makes sense. However, I honestly loved reading each page of both Noah and Echo's journey. <br /><br />I have to say, though I really liked the main characters, the secondary characters were just loathsome. I wanted to bitch-slap Grace so hard!! She is a (insert nasty word HERE). I also didn't forgive Ashley (aka daddy-stealer... what? I would never get over that "I just wanted to be your mom so badly" BULL) and her emotion-void father. <br /><br />I think what pushed this to 5 stars for me was how well the author pulled me into the main character's lives. I was completely invested in their stories and I cared <i>so freaking much</i> about what happened to them. That is saying a lot.<br /><br />When I saw that there was a second book in the series, I was PISSED. I thought it would be a continuation of Echo and Noah's story (which, by the way, would have been totally unnecessary). I was so happy I could have done a little dance when I saw that it was Beth's story instead. Kate McGarry got the memo to leave well enough alone!!! (note: listen up Colleen Hoover!!!). I will most certainly be moving on with this series. <br /><br />**Copy provided by the publisher in exchange for an honest review**</span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1272700454?book_show_action=true">Jul 09, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="NMmomof4" class="user" itemprop="url" name="NMmomof4" href="/user/show/24665574-nmmomof4">NMmomof4</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/24665574-nmmomof4?shelf=safe">safe</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1272700454" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2413234768874096835"><b> 4 Stars</b><br/><br/><b>Overall Opinion: </b>This was actually better than I thought it would be! I get in the mood for some teenage drama every once in a while, and I read a YA book. I'm happy I found this one in one of my trusted GR friend's favorites list! This author goes pretty deeply into these characters, and made me <i>feel</i> for both of them and root for their happiness. Both of them were dealt crappy hands, but they were able to find safety and love in each other. This is a great example of where we aren't giv</span>
  <span id="freeText2413234768874096835" style="display:none"><b> 4 Stars</b><br /><br /><b>Overall Opinion: </b>This was actually better than I thought it would be! I get in the mood for some teenage drama every once in a while, and I read a YA book. I'm happy I found this one in one of my trusted GR friend's favorites list! This author goes pretty deeply into these characters, and made me <i>feel</i> for both of them and root for their happiness. Both of them were dealt crappy hands, but they were able to find safety and love in each other. This is a great example of where we aren't given <i>steam</i>, but there was enough <i>connection</i> to make up for it! My biggest complaint? The ending. I don't know why an epilogue would hurt!! I'm a well known epi-ho, so there is that...<br /><br /><b>Brief Summary of the Storyline: </b> This is Echo and Noah's story. They've known who each other are for a while, but they have to actually be together when Echo is assigned to tutor Noah. They bump heads at first, but they soon find out that they both have a lot going on in their lives that other people in the school have no idea about. Echo has some mysterious scars on her arms that appeared all of a sudden and got her on the outs with the popular crowd she was with, and Noah is a relatively new kid that hangs out with a stoner crowd. They both have been assigned to work with this new clinical social worker in the school to work through their struggles, and they bond through it and fall in love. There is some family and friend drama, some past demons to work through, and some sweet moments...and they get a HFN ending.<br /><br /><b>POV:</b> This alternated between Echo and Noah's POV.<br /><br /><b>Overall Pace of Story: </b> Good. I never skimmed and I thought it flowed well.<br /><br /><b>Instalove:</b> No, but they do move pretty quickly into stronger feelings.<br /><br /><b>H rating:</b> 4.5 stars. Noah. I really liked him. I appreciated how much he cared for his family.<br /><br /><b>h rating:</b> 3.5 stars. Echo. I liked her, but the way she let some people treat her really bugged me (her friends and her dad).<br /><br /><b>Sadness level: </b>Low/moderate. I cried, but I never needed any tissues.<br /><br /><b>Push/Pull:</b> Yes <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Both the h and H push away and pursue the relationship at times.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><b>Heat level:</b> Low. There are some heavy make out sessions, but they never have sex.<br /><br /><b>Descriptive sex:</b> No<br /><br /><b>Safe sex:</b> N/A<br /><br /><b>OW/OM drama:</b> Yes <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[The h's ex tries to get back with her.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><b>Sex scene with OW or OM:</b> No<br /><br /><b>Cheating: </b> No <br /><br /><b>Separation:</b> Yes <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[They are separated for ~3 weeks, but there was no mention or suggestion of other partners during this time.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><b>Possible Triggers: </b>Yes <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Parent with bipolar disorder (h off page - through memories), loss of parents (H off page - through memories), loss of military brother (h off page - through memories), abusive foster homes/being separated from siblings (H off page - through memories), attempted murder of h (off page - through memories), drug use/underage drinking (H and side characters on page), H was a manwhore before h, and h is a virgin.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><b>Closure: </b> This is my biggest complaint about YA (and even some NA) books. I understand that they are young, and we shouldn't necessarily get a HEA with them married with kids -- but why couldn't we at least get a glimpse into their future as adults? Or going to college? Something. I would call this a HFN ending.<br /><br /><b>How I got it:</b> I got it on loan through my public library and Amazon.<br /><br /><b>Safety:</b> This one should be <u>Safe</u> for most safety gang readers<br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[<br />- <b>Does Not</b> have cheating<br />- <b>Does Not</b> have a descriptive sex scene with OW/OM<br />- <b> Does</b> have both the h and H pushing away<br />- <b> Does</b> have a short separation between the h and H<br />- <b> Does</b> have abuse<br />- <b> Does Not</b> have OTT sad parts<br />- <b>Does Not</b> have a HEA ending <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></span>

<div id="review_176769972" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/176769972" />
    <a title="Stephanie " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4795605-stephanie"><img alt="Stephanie " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1339305204p2/4795605.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/176769972?book_show_action=true">Jun 14, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Stephanie " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Stephanie " href="/user/show/4795605-stephanie">Stephanie </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4795605-stephanie?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4795605-stephanie?shelf=no-bueno">no-bueno</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4795605-stephanie?shelf=don-t-believe-the-hype">don-t-believe-the-hype</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4795605-stephanie?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4795605-stephanie?shelf=coming-of-age">coming-of-age</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4795605-stephanie?shelf=realistic-fiction">realistic-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4795605-stephanie?shelf=parent-needs-an-asskickin">parent-needs-an-asskickin</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4795605-stephanie?shelf=mental-health-mental-illness">mental-health-mental-illness</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4795605-stephanie?shelf=disappointment">disappointment</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4795605-stephanie?shelf=insufferable-characters">insufferable-characters</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer176769972" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3580934257910530535">JFC, THIS EFFING BOOK! <br/><br/>I was all set to give it 2.5 stars--generous of me, even--but the resolution of Echo's story was the last straw. Blame and further demonize the already demonized mentally ill mother? Ok, a goddamn <b>1 star</b> for this over dramatized and hollow book! <i>Crucio</i> to you! I am enraged right now and will try to refrain from being an a-hole with this review. <br/><br/>The best thing about <i>Pushing the Limits</i> is that it had an interesting plot: Echo is dealing with the loss of her older brother, ov</span>
  <span id="freeText3580934257910530535" style="display:none">JFC, THIS EFFING BOOK! <br /><br />I was all set to give it 2.5 stars--generous of me, even--but the resolution of Echo's story was the last straw. Blame and further demonize the already demonized mentally ill mother? Ok, a goddamn <b>1 star</b> for this over dramatized and hollow book! <i>Crucio</i> to you! I am enraged right now and will try to refrain from being an a-hole with this review. <br /><br />The best thing about <i>Pushing the Limits</i> is that it had an interesting plot: Echo is dealing with the loss of her older brother, overbearing father, self-centered step-mom, bipolar mother and tenuous high school social status, while trying to remember a traumatic experience she's blacked out of her memory; and Noah, who is trying desperately to reunite what's left of his family--him and his two little brothers--after losing both parents in a house fire a few years ago, separating Noah and his two brothers, as they're placed in different foster homes. Sadly, the execution was a mess, the writing hollow and uninspiring, wrought with misguided metaphors and cheesy analogies, painted ludicrous images of Echo and Noah alike and everyone else related to them. Most of the characters were also one-note and unlikable. I didn't love ANYONE. I liked Noah most times, and merely tolerated Echo. Oh, and Echo's "friends", with the exception of Lila (once in a blue moon), were shit. And that bastard Luke needs a good thump in the face. <br /><br />There was also a whole lot of telling and not enough showing, at least not showing in a way that engaged me as a reader. For me, <i>Pushing the Limits</i> had no heart despite the material being there. The material surely pushed the limits, but unfortunately, McGarry's writing left a lot to be desired. I found reading this novel akin to watching one of those horribly good-bad <i>Lifetime</i> movies. Poor production, acting, soap opera-ry drama, and crap dialogue? It's all here in the book. <br /><br />I was also very much horrified with the way McGarry handled Echo's mom's type-I bipolar disorder. I don't know if she did any research at all about how it affects people, but I'm sure those diagnosed with either type who read this would be offended. After finishing the novel, and knowing where the author left Echo's relationship and opinion of her mother, I almost feel the mental illness was used as a cheap ploy to push the limits of this story all in the name of drama. I was very much hoping there would be a sliver of humanizing Echo's mother (her actions we really farfetched for her type of illness), who was an emotional prisoner to her disease for so long. Better writing, perhaps, could have made that not the case. And the resolution of her not only turning out to be an<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[attempted murderer of her daughter--making Echo ingest a high dose of sleeping pills via iced tea she'd made herself to commit suicide the day of the incident <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>, but also a selfish, grudge holding bitch who doesn't seem to care two shits for her daughter. It was inconceivable. Especially since McGarry spent a good portion of the book with Echo remembering the times her mother did in fact love her and cared. As a reader, you never get a sense for the difficulty Echo's mother had with living with her disease (a difficulty that's not always easy to just write-off the mentally ill person as being psycho and selfish). In that aspect, it made Echo's and everyone else opinion of her mother one-sided, making the whole plot-line, for me, insensitive and a bit contrived.<br /><br />I was all excited to read this because a dear Goodreads friend of mine, whose opinion I'm usually in agreement with, said it was close to a Marchetta book. After reading this, I can tell you that that is utter blasphemy, IMO. Melina Marchetta is a writing goddess (I know, over the top, but SO VERY TRUE!). And although <i>Pushing the Limits</i> deals with family dynamics and relationships, which is Marchetta's signature forte, it doesn't even hold the slightest of candles in resemblance of her work. Sorry to say, friend. <br /><br />But don't believe me. Read it for yourself (my opinion is more so in the minority); though, I'd say borrow it from a friend or the library and spend the money on an actual Marchetta book. <br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="3580934257910530535" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1944145951" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1944145951" />
    <a title="Zain Otoom" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/45136398-zain-otoom"><img alt="Zain Otoom" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1598878687p2/45136398.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1944145951?book_show_action=true">Mar 17, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Zain Otoom" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Zain Otoom" href="/user/show/45136398-zain-otoom">Zain Otoom</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9781460312032" href="/book/show/15326588-pushing-the-limits">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1944145951" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2226275858178399582"><i>"Because growing up means making tough choices, and doing the right thing doesn't necessarily mean doing the thing that feels good."</i><br/>*****<br/>You know it's a good book when you'll never look at certain things the same way. This book was such an unexpectedly good read. I picked it up thinking it was like any cheesy romance book out there. Boy, I was wrong. <br/>Now, I never had to deal with any of the problems that the main characters had to, nor do I know people in real life who had. But I do know that th</span>
  <span id="freeText2226275858178399582" style="display:none"><i>"Because growing up means making tough choices, and doing the right thing doesn't necessarily mean doing the thing that feels good."</i><br />*****<br />You know it's a good book when you'll never look at certain things the same way. This book was such an unexpectedly good read. I picked it up thinking it was like any cheesy romance book out there. Boy, I was wrong. <br />Now, I never had to deal with any of the problems that the main characters had to, nor do I know people in real life who had. But I do know that the author dealt with these problems quite realistically. It was really hard sometimes to read because of all the mess going on. My heart would be teared into pieces just reading certain chapters. <br />I teared up a couple of times, but I also smiled widely many times; especially at the end. <br /><b>I love it when characters grow.</b><br />Not to mention, this book does send out some really great messages, but I like feel mentioning them would be a spoiler. Besides, not everyone get the same experience reading the same book. You'll probably latch on specific things that will stand out to you. <br />Why one star off? Well, I wanted a different kind of romance in this book, one that suited the tone of it. It felt off sometimes. <br />But don't take that as a con. Honestly, just ignore the romance and focus on the other things that this book gives you.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2226275858178399582" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer18210995964948503223">That was great. When I started this book I thought it would be some kind of cliché story about a good girl and a bad boy. But surprisingly it turned out to be way more. So much more. <br/>The thing that impressed me the most were the character. As I said I was expecting cliché and one dimensional characters, but they weren’t. They were complex and they had their own stories and problems to overcome.   <span id="freeText18210995964948503223" style="display:none">That was great. When I started this book I thought it would be some kind of cliché story about a good girl and a bad boy. But surprisingly it turned out to be way more. So much more. <br />The thing that impressed me the most were the character. As I said I was expecting cliché and one dimensional characters, but they weren’t. They were complex and they had their own stories and problems to overcome. I love how they helped each other and how deeply they cared for each other. <br />They had a great relationship. I absolutely loved them together. <br />Also their family stories were very well developed. The messed up story with her mother, her relationship with her father, her stepmother, her brother, her friends and that’s only Echo’s. Noah has lots of family problems as well. I find it really impressive the author was able to develop her characters in such a great way in such a small book.<br />I really liked this book. I’m going to read the next one for sure.<br /></span>

<div id="review_306520380" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/306520380" />
    <a title="Annie Brewer" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5315988-annie-brewer"><img alt="Annie Brewer" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442496062p2/5315988.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/306520380?book_show_action=true">Apr 04, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Annie Brewer" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Annie Brewer" href="/user/show/5315988-annie-brewer">Annie Brewer</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">All romance lovers</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5315988-annie-brewer?shelf=absolutely-amazingly-awesome">absolutely-amazingly-awesome</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5315988-annie-brewer?shelf=angst">angst</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5315988-annie-brewer?shelf=favorite">favorite</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5315988-annie-brewer?shelf=tearjerker">tearjerker</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5315988-annie-brewer?shelf=books-on-my-shelf">books-on-my-shelf</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5315988-annie-brewer?shelf=irresistable-hot-guys">irresistable-hot-guys</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer306520380" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8717301991482662319">A MILLION STARS FOR THIS BOOK!!!!!! OMG, my emotions are all over the place!! I thought My Life Next Door was my favorite of this year, but HOLY HELL SHIT this book tops it....only by a little. But ummmmm, NOAH HUTCHINS IS MY NEW HOT SEXY BOOK BOYFRIEND. JESUS CHRIST I CAN EAT HIM UP!!!!!! I need a day to collect my thoughts before a proper review. So I am just going to say, well done Katie!!!! This was FANTASTIC!!!!<br/><br/>Full review soon!<br/><br/><br/>Edited review:<br/><br/>I have no idea where to begin with this review, m</span>
  <span id="freeText8717301991482662319" style="display:none">A MILLION STARS FOR THIS BOOK!!!!!! OMG, my emotions are all over the place!! I thought My Life Next Door was my favorite of this year, but HOLY HELL SHIT this book tops it....only by a little. But ummmmm, NOAH HUTCHINS IS MY NEW HOT SEXY BOOK BOYFRIEND. JESUS CHRIST I CAN EAT HIM UP!!!!!! I need a day to collect my thoughts before a proper review. So I am just going to say, well done Katie!!!! This was FANTASTIC!!!!<br /><br />Full review soon!<br /><br /><br />Edited review:<br /><br />I have no idea where to begin with this review, my emotions are still very raw since I turned the last page of this book. But I will begin with the cover.....I LOVE THIS FREAKIN COVER. There are two different versions of this book. I got the hardback book the day it came out. OMG, as soon as it came out I was there. I called up my B&amp;N and asked them to put this book on hold for me cause I was halling ass up there to get it! I feel like there was a wave of de ja vu. When I had this book in my hands, I clutched it to my chest and breathed in the book. Silly I know. But seriously, those two on the cover resemble very closely Noah and Echo. The other version is on ereader and I don't like that one as much. I am happy with the cover I've got. I mean look at them. First of all, the guy is smokin HOT and his position practically thrusting her up against the locker. Come on, that says enough right there. Oh yeah, I love it. And she's all leaning into him with her foot on the locker, supporting her. If I was her, I wouldn't be able to keep from collapsing with him that close. Damn! Anyway, you get the point, I love the book cover.<br /><br />When I first heard of this book, I was all over it. I looked up reviews and so many reviews raved about this book. I also noticed ALOT of comparison to Simone Elkles' Perfect Chemistry. And if you know me well enough, you know how much I devoured that book. SO it was a safe bet that I would love this book just as much. But guess what? I love this book even MORE!!! I'll always love my Alex Fuentes....but my heart has now found Noah Hutchins and I can't help but say, HOLY SHIT! He will rock your world, I promise!<br /><br />So now to get on with my review. <br /><br />Echo Emerson lost everything the night her brother died in Afghanistan and she woke up in the hospital with no recollection of what happened to her...except the scars on her arms now her mom has a restraining order against her. She walks the halls like a zombie and is scared to be hersef around her friends that were there for her before the incident. Now they turn their back on her because she is different. They treat her like an outsider. She was dating popular boy Luke and when it got to be too much for her, she broke it off and quit going to school.<br />Her dad wanted her to get help. So she starts seeing social worker Mrs. Collins who tries everything she can to help Echo remember what happened that night that tore her family apart. Once she remembers, she might feel better and can finally sleep in peace for the first time in 2 years. In the mean time, she tutors a boy for chemistry, who is not much different than her....<br /><br />Noah lost everything the night of the house fire 2 years earlier, which claimed his parents. His brothers were taken away and he was bouncing from foster family to foster family. Until Mrs. Collins became his social worker, claiming she could help him get his life back on track. Getting tutored by Echo was the last thing he expected...but maybe it was the best thing that ever happened to him. Together they worked to get answers about their past, that might help them both heal and face a future that is unknown. But can they do it together or will it shatter their world even more?<br /><br />WOW, when I finished this book last night, I felt numb. I'm not saying there wasn't an HEA and I'm not saying there is. I'm saying from the moment I opened the book and started the first page, I felt every emotion from giddy, happy, funny, angry, sad, confused, back to angry, sad and everything inbetween. There were so many emotions going through me at once that it became hard to distinguish which emotion I was actually going through. The fact that both characters were facing such tough choices in their lives, it made my heart ache for them so badly. They started off kind of hostile toward each other. Noah felt that Echo was just this selfish, princess bitch that always got her way. And Echo assumed that Noah was this pot smoking, drinker asshole bad boy that everyone made him out to be. Their relationship grew slowly and intense once they realized that they were so much alike. They were both struggling with demons of their own, but trying to be themselves in the process. Noah was the sweetest, most wonderful guy Echo could have ever met. He supported her and even when he saw her ugly scars that covered her arms, he never turned away. Not once. And he even told her she was still beautiful. No one ever treated her the way Noah did. It was so beaituful to see their relationship blossom and intensify as time went on. I cried, laughed,smiled, cursed, pulled my hair, yelled at Noah, told some of them off throughout the book. There were some unexpected twists and dammit if I wasn't already distraught. Katie threw in some really crazy and sad shit in there. For giggles? I don't know, but I wasn't laughing. I cried so hard, I had to stop a few times to collect myself cause I couldn't see the pages. I understood their pain, losing a parent is never easy. My heart ached the whole way through with Noah. I wanted to hug him. Then at one point he tries getting custody of his 2 younger brothers once he graduates high school. OMG, that whole situation with that was hard to deal with. I had a hard time breathing, seeing the pain Noah went through. All he wanted was his brothers together again, their family minus their parents. And when you learn the truth about what happened that night, you're just even more broken up about it! It is truly sad!<br /><br />I loved all of the secondary characters. Noah's best friends Beth and Isaiah were amazing! They were such good friends and support for Noah. They really looked after him and stuck by him, even when they were unsure about Echo. Beth kinda ticked me off at times. But I realized it was only to protect Noah's heart. I grew to love her.<br />I only liked Lila, Echo's best friend. Even though at first she pissed me off, she turned her shit around and showed her better side.I hate Grace and Luke and all the rest that were so judgmental and hateful. Little bastards! I punch their faces in! I loved when Noah and Luke fought at the dance. OMG, I was rooting for him to beat the shit out of Luke. Yeah, I'm volitile. Oh well.<br />I liked Echo's dad and her step mom, eventhough there was alot of drama with that. But OMG I wanted to kill her fucking mom!!!! I felt bad for her. I really did. But when I found out the truth, HOLY FUCKING SHIT, I wanted to slap myself for feeling sorry for that horrible bitch! I loved Noah's little brothers. OMG, my heart hurt for them. Their foster parents really warmed my heart but I still felt a stab of sadness for Noah because he wanted to adopt them so badly. But in the end, things worked out for the best. And my favorite character in this, Mrs. Collins...she was the glue to the whole thing. She was amazing! She never gave up on either of them. She showed them that to trust and put faith first, things will aways work out. I loved her so much for everything she did for them! Ugh, its bringing on the waterworks again! Just thinking about this book, makes me want to sob all over again. It was a beautiful story about love, friendship, trust, starting over, healing, and moving on. <br /><br />The end. Oh my the ending was AMAZING! I loved it so much! Seriously, this book brought out so many raw emotions from me. I highly recommend this book to all romance lovers. Trust me, this book will consume you. And you'll be left thinking about it long after you turn the last page!! So all you PC fans, prepare for a story that will rock you, sock you, knock you on your ass! It's truly SPECTACULAR!!!! I am definitely reading more from this author!! Fantastic debut Mrs. McGarry!!!!</span>
  <a data-text-id="8717301991482662319" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

    <a title="Exina" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5309539-exina"><img alt="Exina" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1580809437p2/5309539.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/413700167?book_show_action=true">Sep 13, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Exina" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Exina" href="/user/show/5309539-exina">Exina</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5309539-exina?shelf=long-winded-wordy">long-winded-wordy</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5309539-exina?shelf=teens">teens</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5309539-exina?shelf=complex-characters">complex-characters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5309539-exina?shelf=dual-pov">dual-pov</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5309539-exina?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5309539-exina?shelf=emotional">emotional</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5309539-exina?shelf=expected-more">expected-more</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5309539-exina?shelf=family">family</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5309539-exina?shelf=first-love">first-love</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer413700167" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16778779469456722119"><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>I’d lost and I’d won. I’d lost the dreams I had, but won new dreams.</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br/>It was way too long. I have to admit that I skipped several descriptive parts, and focused on only dialogues. Maybe I’m too old to enjoy wholeheartedly Young Adult fiction…<br/><br/>Anyway, the novel tries to represent serious values and moral issues, such as love, trust, respect, forgiveness, sacrifice, and selflessness. It also deals with grief, drug use, hasty sex, child abuse and abandonment. But the writing is elongated, </span>
  <span id="freeText16778779469456722119" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>I’d lost and I’d won. I’d lost the dreams I had, but won new dreams.</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>It was way too long. I have to admit that I skipped several descriptive parts, and focused on only dialogues. Maybe I’m too old to enjoy wholeheartedly Young Adult fiction…<br><br>Anyway, the novel tries to represent serious values and moral issues, such as love, trust, respect, forgiveness, sacrifice, and selflessness. It also deals with grief, drug use, hasty sex, child abuse and abandonment. But the writing is elongated, repetitive, over-explained. Is this didactic writing really necessary for younger readers to understand the message of the story?<br><br>Both the main characters and the secondary characters are likeable. Echo and Noah both had serious traumas, and I really felt for them.<br><br>Echo’s character develops nicely throughout the story. At the beginning her behavior is very self-oriented, her fear of gossip is exaggerated. But her attitude changes by the end of the story. She is able to forgive her father and Ashley, but she easily oversteps the love she feels for her mother. The main part of the story is about that how Echo loves her mother, misses her mother, adores her mother, etc. And after only a short conversation, Echo determines that her mother doesn’t deserve her love any more.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1483569047i/21626316.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Noah’s character is the typical bad boy: sweet, charming, but clichéd, using over-the-top annoying endearments for Echo (baby, siren, etc.).<br><blockquote>
  <i>"One month before school lets out—she disappears.” Beth’s eyes widened and she spread her fingers out like a magician doing a trick.<br>Isaiah nodded. “Poof.”<br>“Gone,” added Beth.<br>“Vanished,” said Isaiah.<br>“Lost.”<br>“Evaporated.”<br>“Gone,” repeated Beth. Her eyes glazed over and she stared down at her toes.<br>“Beth,” I prodded.<br>She blinked. “What?”<br>“The story.” This was the problem with hanging out with stoners. “Echo. Continue.”<br>“Oh, yeah, so she disappeared,” said Beth.<br>“Poof,” added Isaiah.<br>Not this again. “I got it. Moving along.”</i>
</blockquote><br>Noah has great moments of course, but a very important thing is missing: what about his guilt about his parents’ death? Is it evaporated? Vanished? Gone? Poof?<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1483569047i/21626317.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>All in all, it is definitely not for me – of course I’m not the target audience – but I can imagine it could be an enjoyable book for YA readers.<br><br><b>
  <a href="http://exinasreadings.tumblr.com/tagged/Pushing-the-Limits" rel="nofollow noopener">My favorite quotes.</a>
</b></span>

<div id="review_385270050" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/385270050" />
    <a title="Brigid" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3973089-brigid"><img alt="Brigid" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1563651379p2/3973089.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/385270050?book_show_action=true">Aug 06, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Brigid" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Brigid" href="/user/show/3973089-brigid">Brigid</a>
      </span>

          added it




        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer385270050" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1114561643444539768">I bought this book the day it came out. I mean, it had EVERYTHING I love in a book: hot boy, attitude, brothers, family drama, romance. I'm surprised there wasn't a neon sign on Goodreads screaming, "BRIGID KEMMERER, YOU NEED TO READ THIS BOOK."<br/><br/>I tore through the first half. I was tempted to hide it under the table at a business conference. (I didn't. Though I did hide it under the table at a book signing this weekend. Shh.) The book made me cry, the book made me smile ... there was definitely a</span>
  <span id="freeText1114561643444539768" style="display:none">I bought this book the day it came out. I mean, it had EVERYTHING I love in a book: hot boy, attitude, brothers, family drama, romance. I'm surprised there wasn't a neon sign on Goodreads screaming, "BRIGID KEMMERER, YOU NEED TO READ THIS BOOK."<br /><br />I tore through the first half. I was tempted to hide it under the table at a business conference. (I didn't. Though I did hide it under the table at a book signing this weekend. Shh.) The book made me cry, the book made me smile ... there was definitely an emotional reaction to some of the events. <br /><br />That said, I can't decide on a star rating. And not like I can't decide between a 4 and a 5. I'm all over the map on this one. Each time I reach to click on a star, I'm like, "No, but wait..." Some of the relationships between people were SO AMAZING (like between Noah and his friends) but then others were so ... vague (like between Echo and Ashley), and I just can't decide where this one's going to fall. There's some great writing here, and I loved Noah as a character. I think he was fantastically written. Buuuuuuut then I spent half the book wanting to smack him. I even had an hour long chat with a friend last night about this book, and I *still* can't decide how to rate it. I'd say I'm going to leave it unrated because I don't want to skew another author's rating, but really, it's just because I don't know what to click. :-) <br /><br />This book is getting huge buzz (well-deserved, I might add), so there are many, many other reviews to read that will give you a better picture of whether you'll like it. I definitely recommend it as a book to read, whether you like Simone Elkeles' Perfect Chemistry series, or Alex Flinn's books (her earlier stuff, not the recent paranormal fairy-tale stuff), or any kind of issue-heavy, edgy, YA Contemporary. <br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="1114561643444539768" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer371567206" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1372606583165989634">I need to put this book down for the time being. I'm at 40% and I know this is an excellent book, but the subject matter is very serious, sad, and quite depressing. I'm in the mood for a lighter, happier read. I can tell this is one of the better young adult books written and <b>I want to give it the change it deserves</b>. I just need to be in the right mood to read it. </span>

          </span>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('xIhPw3DNZVzrBHoYUQcN5dMjsyYyDtDmBxAZotFI/oL8wEc05V7wmOH96xk2q8IUxTH45qfDiIJiiQiuuRtcGA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('6O6NF9VIBtSi5vuVJvrst4giYmh5k4SYIdPlhKbu9pzQpoXgQNuTEKgfapRBViNGnjApqOxe3PxESvSIzr1UBg==')})
  }
